### Post by Shpongle on 2009-04-30
> * Stay within the board rules, no matter how hot you may believe the wallpaper/screen shot to be.
* If you are going to quote, there isn't a need to quote an img-embeded picture - Just don't do it. Please just reference the post by page number/page link/etc.
* Off Topic Posts will be edited or removed.
* The desktops thread is not to be used as a means to post explicit or suggestive, and provocative images (they must be safe for your kids and/or boss to see). Please help to keep the thread relevant and safe to browse for everyone.
* The moderators of this forum reserve the right to edit or remove your posts as necessary so they may comply with our Community Rule set.
* Please use reduced-size thumbnails, where possible, out of respect for people running on lower bandwidth or screen resolutions.
* To avoid having users having to ask you for them. we request that you format your posts in the following order:

Themes: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Wallpaper: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Icons: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Programs: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).
Important Note: Any image posted that is over 800 x 600 will be removed! Use a thumbnail or use a text link to your image. If your image is removed, this is why.

heres mine for may :)
theme aurora leopard bsm light
icons mac ultimate leopard
wallpaper deviant art search for open source

### Post by myxiplx on 2009-05-01
Well here's mine.  This is my first attempt at really customizing my desktop, after discovering conky two days ago.  My conky is largely inspired by Jecho's setup:
[http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=7174389&postcount=1419](http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=7174389&postcount=1419)

Overall it's two screens, 4 desktops, and a two line taskbar since I have a bad habbit of keeping way too many programs running :)

### Post by unoodles on 2009-05-01
Here's mine. The idea is that everything on my desktop has to be black and white, except there is hints of blue in certain places. Opening windows uses the burn effect, with blue flame. Closing windows uses the beam-up effect coloured blue.

Following this theme, I use the [black-white 2 style icons]("http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/black-white+2+Style?content=72619")
The GTK+ theme is [darklooks]("http://packages.ubuntu.com/jaunty/gnome-themes-extras") (in gnome-themes-extra)
Fonts are all [ttf-droid]("http://packages.ubuntu.com/jaunty/ttf-droid").

---

### Post by Giant Speck on 2009-05-01
> **perfectska04 said:**
> What userstyle/theme did you use to get those awesome firefox tabs?

[B]Make tabs appear as buttons:

[/B]```
@namespace url(http://www.mozilla.org/keymaster/gatekeeper/there.is.only.xul);
.tabbrowser-arrowscrollbox + stack {
  display: none !important;
}


@-moz-document url(chrome://browser/content/browser.xul) {
  tab {
    padding: 0 !important;
    margin-top: -1px !important;
    margin-bottom: 1px !important;
    margin-left: 1px !important;
  }

  tab:not([selected="true"]) {
    -moz-appearance: button !important;
  }

  tab:not([selected="true"]) > .tab-middle {
    /* you can change the background color of active tab here */
  }

  tab[selected="true"] {
    -moz-appearance: button !important;
    margin-left: 0 !important;
    padding-left: 0px !important;
  }

  tab[selected="true"] > .tab-middle {
    background-color: #efeee9;
  }

  tab:focus > .tab-middle {
    outline: none !important;
  }
}
```

[B]Change tab close button

[/B]```
@namespace url(http://www.mozilla.org/keymaster/gatekeeper/there.is.only.xul);



/* Tab close button */
.tab-close-button > .toolbarbutton-icon {
  -moz-margin-end: 0px !important;
  margin-top: 0px;
}

.tab-close-button,
.close-button.tabs-closebutton > .toolbarbutton-icon {
;
  -moz-margin-end: 0px;
  border: none;
  padding: 0px;
  list-style-image: url("data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAABAAAAAQCAYAAAAf8/9hAAAAGXRFWHRTb2Z0d2FyZQBBZG9iZSBJ

6In2h99jNNgAAAAASUVORK5CYII=") !important;

```

[B]Lower inactive tab visibility:

[/B]```
tab[selected="false"] {
  opacity: .4 !important;
}

tab[selected="false"]:hover {
  opacity: 1 !important;
}

tab[selected="true"] {
  opacity: 1 !important;
}
```

It has taken me a while and a lot of searching on Userstyles.org to get things just right.  The only thing I wish is that I could make the tabs thinner without squashing the close button.  I've tried Slim Tabs, but it didn't work correctly.

### Post by Giant Speck on 2009-05-02
> **vishzilla said:**
> how did you get your bookmarks in the menu bar?
 
Right click the bookmarks bar and click "Customize."  Then drag the text that says "Bookmark Items" and drag it up to the menubar.  Once you've done that, exit the customize window and right-click again to remove the bookmark toolbar.

---

### Post by vishzilla on 2009-05-02
> **Giant Speck said:**
> Right click the bookmarks bar and click "Customize."  Then drag the text that says "Bookmark Items" and drag it up to the menubar.  Once you've done that, exit the customize window and right-click again to remove the bookmark toolbar.

cool. quite simple :)

### Post by Russell Burrows on 2009-05-02
Wow.
All those desktops are very cool.

All I have on my desktop is a single menu icon and a single folder icon that are very small.

My desktop images are just playing an anime, action, sci fi, horror or kids movie and hitting pause on a scene I like then I select take snapshot and that image ends up being my desktop wallpaper image of the day or sometimes the hour.

For example yesterday we were watching the movie Advent Children that I got on blu ray and I was running the backup copy on the laptop and out to the HDTV when a pal says that Clouds motorcycle is huge and I say yeah nice desktop image and my pals say that movie is just out so forget about getting any wallpapers since the movie is so recent.

So I just went back frame by frame and then just hit take snapshot and viola! wallpaper!

It works even for snapshots of Nova episodes and other shows as long as its a video file its easy to get a snapshot and pow! instant cool desktop.

Panel (xfce4-panel), left to right: Xfce Menu (w/ Command division icon), Places, Action Buttons (Lock Screen), Launcher (w/ Federation pin icon), Task List, Disk Mounter (xfapplet), Screenshooter, Volume Applet (xfapplet), Notification Area, Clock (xfapplet)
Overall icon theme: OSX_Aluminum (see [Xfce-Look]("http://http://xfce-look.org/content/show.php/OSX_Aluminium?content=99140") - it goes better with the theme)
Menu and appfinder icons: [http://iconfactory.com/startrek/](http://iconfactory.com/startrek/) (converted to png with ImageMagick)

#83aa7a

#own_window_colour black

xftfont Existence-45

${color}Cpu: ${color0}${cpu}%
${color}Mem: ${color0}$memperc%
${color}/: ${color0}${fs_used_perc /}%${color}, /data: ${color0}${fs_used_perc /media/data}%${color}, /ext: ${color0}${fs_used_perc /media/ext}%

### Post by supersonicdarky on 2009-05-02
> **el mariachi said:**
> could you also share the weather script? I can't find that version (I only find terribly complicated ones:S) thanks a lot :)
```
#!/usr/bin/python

import urllib, re, sys, os

weather={}

def checkConnection(url):
	return not os.system("ping "+url+" -c 1 > /dev/null")
	
def usage():
	print "usage: weather.py <citycode> <system> <what>"
	print "\t<citycode>: can be retrieved from weather.com"
	print "\t<system>: c or f"
	print "\t<what>: what do you want printed"
	print "\t\tt: current temp"
	print "\t\tw: wind speed/direction"
	print "\t\th: humidity"
	print "\t\tc: current conditions"
	
def fileExists(f):
	try:
		file = open(f)
		return True
	except IOError:
		return False
		
def printWeather(x):
	try:
 		if x == 't': print weather['temp']
		if x == 'w': print weather['wind']+"/h"
		if x == 'h': print weather['humi']+"%"
		if x == 'c': print weather['cond']
	except:
		print "?"
	
def parseWeather(location):
	tmp = open(location).read()
	temp = re.compile(".*?<div class=\"forecast-temp\">.*?\n.*?<h3>(-?\\d\\d?)\°</h3>.*?",re.DOTALL).match(tmp)
	humi = re.compile(".*?<dt>Humidity:</dt><dd>(\\d\\d?)%.*?",re.DOTALL).match(tmp)
	wind = re.compile(".*?<dt>Wind:</dt><dd>(\\D\\D? \\d\\d? \\D)ph.*?",re.DOTALL).match(tmp)
	cond = re.compile(".*?<em>Current conditions.*?\n.*?<h3>(.*?)</h3>.*?",re.DOTALL).match(tmp)
	
	if temp: weather['temp'] = temp.group(1)
	if humi: weather['humi'] = humi.group(1)
	if wind: weather['wind'] = wind.group(1)
	if cond: weather['cond'] = cond.group(1)
	
		
if len(sys.argv)==4 and re.compile("\\D*?\\d*?").match(sys.argv[1]) and re.compile("[cf]").match(sys.argv[2]) and re.compile("[twch]").match(sys.argv[3]):
	code = sys.argv[1]
	unit = sys.argv[2]
	display = sys.argv[3]
	location = "http://weather.yahoo.com/forecast/"+code+"_"+unit+".html"
	store = "/tmp/tmp_weather"
	if checkConnection("www.google.com"):
		urllib.urlretrieve(location, store)
		parseWeather(store)
		printWeather(display)
	elif not checkConnection("www.google.com") and fileExists(store):
		parseWeather(store)
		printWeather(display)
	
	exit
else:
	usage()
	exit
```

Something I wrote back in my early days of python. Could definitely be improved, but I have no motivation to do so :p

### Post by perfectska04 on 2009-05-05
> **Giant Speck said:**
> Hmm... I can't figure out how you got the simple down arrow in the address bar in Firefox instead of the default Murrine button.

You can use the following CSS to imitate the Firefox 3.5 urlbar, I've been using it for the shiki-colors userstyle for a while:
```
/* Awesomebar improvements */

#urlbar {
    -moz-appearance: textfield !important;
}

#urlbar .autocomplete-textbox-container {
    background-color: -moz-Field !important;
    -moz-appearance: none !important;
}

#urlbar > .autocomplete-history-dropmarker {
    -moz-appearance: toolbarbutton-dropdown !important;
    margin: 0px 3px 0px 5px !important;
}
```

---

### Post by perfectska04 on 2009-05-05
> **walkerk said:**
> Very nice. Thanks for this :)

No problem. You can also use the Shiki-Colors firefox userstyle. It adds the Firefox 3.5 urlbar, adds support for fission extension, and fixes other annoyances in dark and hybrid themes (such as dust and newwave dark) that the firefox devs should have added in the first place.
[http://userstyles.org/styles/10822](http://userstyles.org/styles/10822)

> **Giant Speck said:**
> That is awesome.  Now if only you can figure out how to remove that ugly border that Firefox puts around the awesome bar when you use it with a dark theme.  The only way I can think of is to create a pixmap, but I don't know how to replace the awesomebar with a pixmap using CSS.

Yeah, those white borders are annoying as hell. I've not been able to fix them at all. There are, however, a few ways around it:
1. Upgrade to firefox 3.5 (I tested it and it seems to be fixed there).
2. Use an older version of clearlooks or murrine (the ones that came with Hardy don't have this issue).
3. Copy the CSS code from an existing firefox theme, such as Dust. You'll have to edit the pixmaps in GIMP, though.
4. Use the pixmaps engine to draw GTK entries, like NewWave.

---

### Post by Mazza558 on 2009-05-07
Work in progress for a new UI setup I have going. Supports around 15-16 individual applications other than those already in Docky, before Docky starts to overlap the notification area. However, I cannot think of any situation where I'd be running 17+ applications simultaneously - individual windows of applications are grouped so this isn't a problem. I can scroll through the windows contained within an application using the scroll wheel in docky.

I use scale for the top left corner, making Window Management easy. I'm keeping this setup for a long, long time (with tweaks). 

Things to do include:

- Change mint menu logo (I'm using Ubuntu Jaunty)
- See if I can shrink the garish Notification area icons somehow.

### Post by rjmdomingo2003 on 2009-05-08
> **emissman said:**
> Thanks! 

Any chance I can leach your Conky config? I've been using the Screenlets weather but those things are sort of buggy it seems.

Sure

```
own_window no
own_window_type normal
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_hints undecorate,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager
double_buffer yes
short_units yes
use_xft yes
update_interval 2
draw_shades no
draw_outline no
xftfont AvantGardeLTMedium:bold:pixelsize=16
minimum_size 1280 0
default_color fae474
alignment top_left
gap_x 15
gap_y 15

TEXT
${font AvantGardeLTMedium:pixelsize=8}${execi 1800 python ~/scripts/conkyForecast.py --location=AEXX0004 --datatype=CC}
${font}${voffset -6}${execi 1800 python ~/scripts/conkyForecast.py --location=AEXX0004 --datatype=HT}${font AvantGardeLTMedium:bold:pixelsize=8}${color a9a28f}
${voffset -1}${cpugraph cpu1 10,40}
${cpugraph cpu2 10,40}${color}
${offset 12}${voffset -23}${cpu cpu1}%
${offset 12}${cpu cpu2}%
${voffset -2}${font AvantGardeLTMedium:pixelsize=6}${execi 3600 remind '-kecho %s'}
```

You have to look at [this]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=869328&highlight=conky+weather") first though.

### Post by MurkMenthaa on 2009-05-09
Here's Mine (see attachment)

Graphs in conky need a little work, cant read texts above them with ease.
Desktop icons only show when you click on them; Its a glitch I guess due to conky, but I like it this way better :p

Anyone know a command that gives % memory usage so I can use it like I'm using it with those icons before 'Root :' & 'Home :' ?
What I did there is take ten's place of % use of / & /home from df (like '8' from '87%') and display it in pie chart fonts.
```
${font Pie charts for maps:size=14}${execi 30 df | grep "/dev/sda5" | cut -c53}${font}
```One more thing, can I make those screenlets in bottom left somehow un-clickable.. or even better, click-though-able ?

Edit:
Umm, think I'm not supposed to ask questions in here, please ignore them in that case.

### Post by el mariachi on 2009-05-09
aaaaaaaaaand.... what's the veredict? :P never tried a tiling manager

---

### Post by elmer_42 on 2009-05-09
It's pretty interesting. I like the way it handles windows; you can place them by holding shift and pressing a number on the keypad. They use the term [gravity]("http://unexist.scrapping.cc/wiki/subtle/Gravity"). Because of this, it's unlike other tiling WMs I've used. Their describe the system (as found [here]("http://unexist.scrapping.cc/wiki/subtle/Subtle")) like this: *The screen is divided into a grid and clients are placed into it. The placement of windows can be controlled either via tags or directly modified with grabs.* I've only been using it for a few minutes, but it's very easy to use. It's in the AUR [here]("http://aur.archlinux.org/packages.php?ID=13016").

It might be easier to get used to this WM than others simply because of the gravity system. If you want to get started, the ArchWiki has a nice page about it [here]("http://wiki.archlinux.org/index.php/Subtle"). The official quickstart page is located on the subtle wiki [here]("http://unexist.scrapping.cc/wiki/subtle/Quickstart"), but the ArchWiki page looks more helpful if you're just trying to get it working quickly.

---

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2009-05-09
> **Doomsword said:**
> Hi, can you share your conky (rss + bottom panel) config? Thank you so much in advance :-)

FabioHaven't gotten around to updating my generic-fonts RSS config so if you want the RSS icon proper, nick it out of the second code frame:
```
own_window_title conkyrss

max_user_text 20000

use_xft yes
xftfont Sans:size=6
override_utf8_locale yes
xftalpha 1

update_interval 1
draw_shades no
default_shade_color 2525ff
draw_outline no
default_outline_color 2525ff
draw_borders no
stippled_borders no
border_margin 0
border_width 1

no_buffers yes
uppercase no
double_buffer yes
use_spacer none

default_color ffffff
color0 ffffff
color1 cfdfdf
color2 bfbfbf
color3 0a0a0a
color4 080808

own_window yes
own_window_colour 080808
own_window_transparent no
own_window_type dock
own_window_hints undecorate,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager,below
background yes
alignment bottom_left
gap_x 1
gap_y 20
minimum_size 1440 0

TEXT
${voffset -3}

gap_y -37

### Post by Vexed Arcanist on 2009-05-10
> **MurkMenthaa said:**
> What's that panel ?

> **sunexplodes said:**
> Looks like tint2.

> **m_duck said:**
> It does, also the tint config is open in the second screenie.

Indeed, it is tint2.

> **pt123 said:**
> Very crisp. 
Would you be able to post your conkyrc file?
Thanks

Sure thing.  Some minor changes were made in the order of system info results, but  you can change all that around.  Note:  I use a large display, changing font size on the clock will likely require changing voffset, offset and goto entries in order to achieve the desired look.

```

background yes
use_xft yes
xftfont Yanone Kaffeesatz:size=16
xftalpha 1
update_interval 1.0
total_run_times 0
own_window yes
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_type desktop
own_window_hints undecorated,below,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager
double_buffer yes
minimum_size 280 200
maximum_width 320
draw_shades no
draw_outline no
draw_borders no
draw_graph_borders no
default_color 122C3D
default_shade_color black
default_outline_color white
alignment top_right
gap_x 22
gap_y 12
no_buffers yes
uppercase no
cpu_avg_samples 2
override_utf8_locale no
TEXT

${goto 30}${font Yanone Kaffeesatz:size=96}${time %H}${voffset -48}${font Yanone Kaffeesatz:bold:size=38}${time :%M}${voffset -18}${font Yanone Kaffeesatz:bold:size=18}${time %S}       

${goto 150}${voffset -10}${font Yanone Kaffeesatz:size=18}${time %A}      
${goto 150}${voffset -4}${time %d %B %Y}  

$mixerbar

${voffset -14}Uptime:$alignr$uptime
CPU1:$alignr${cpu cpu1}%
CPU2:$alignr${cpu cpu2}%
Swap usage:$alignr$swap/$swapmax
RAM:$alignr$mem/$memmax
Windows 7:$alignr${fs_used /media/sda2}/${fs_size /media/sda2}
#!  Linux:$alignr${fs_used /}/${fs_size /}

```

### Post by raul_ on 2009-05-10
> **OutOfReach said:**
> Very nice. How's KDE 4.3 coming so far? Any major improvements/features?

It has many user-noticeable new features since 4.2.
Some new effects are added, better previews on dolphin, dashboard support (widgets separate from desktop), better system tray, etc, etc...

I like it :popcorn:

you can keep track of the new features here:
[techbase.kde.org/Schedules]("techbase.kde.org/Schedules")

click "feature plan" ;)

### Post by marcuskoze on 2009-05-11
Oki doki, here's my spartan desktop setup that I have for 3 years or so and never changed it, except the icon themes (from mac4lin to Oxygen Refit 2)

**Theme:** AquaAdvanced-R (gnome-look.org), combined with "Glider" "form" controls
**Icon Theme:** Oxygen Refit 2 (gnome-look.org)
**Wallpaper:** some mac (obviously) from the Mac4Lin wallpaper package version 3.something, I've never got to actually change the apple with a huge and shiny gnome foot :)
**Additions:** Gnome Global Menu ( [http://code.google.com/p/gnome2-globalmenu](http://code.google.com/p/gnome2-globalmenu) )

Firefox uses iFox Smooth theme (addons.mozilla.com , just give a search for it's name) and TinyMenu plugin... lot's of space in there :)

Other than that, I've added an extra panel on the right with auto-hide option enabled and modified visible size to 1 pixel not to be too intrusive ... so it holds the Menu Bar applet and some other secondary shortcuts like mail clients, GPrename and System Monitor ... 

The main panels have an image as background that I've made with GIMP years ago and never changed my habits about it :) as smooth as possible

---

### Post by nothingspecial on 2009-05-11
It`s not openbox, its standard gnome. The wallpaper is one the highest rated on gnome-look, 1st page I think.

There are 2 ways of doing it. The cheats version is to remove the bottom panel and set the top`s autohide size to 1 with gconf-editor. That way you still get your notifications and can call the menu with Alt F1. - But that`s for cissys.

To truly have nothing to click you have to remove gnome-panel from /usr/bin/. I said move not delete - you might want it back.

Gnome-do is essential and a good knowledge of your keyboard shortcuts. Then I use that groovy fullscreen transparent terminal thingy

[[IMG]http://www.picamatic.com/show/2009/05/11/07/22/3606294_bigthumb.png[/IMG]](http://www.picamatic.com/view/3606294_Screenshot-1/)

And as little window decoration and as few taskbars as possible

[[IMG]http://www.picamatic.com/show/2009/05/11/07/43/3606520_bigthumb.png[/IMG]](http://www.picamatic.com/view/3606520_Screenshot-2/)

Death to the mouse - Outlaw clicking!  :P

---

### Post by eightmillion on 2009-05-11
> **pwnst*r said:**
> gorgeous.
Thanks.
> **Hellow said:**
> I have to wonder what that "Now Playing" script in the bottom-left corner is? Also, what theme is in use here? It all looks awesome.

> **cookieofdoom said:**
> Someone has probably asked you this before, but I can't find it... what are you using to display NowPlaying on your desktop and in your panel?

Thanks.

About the setup, I'm still using Bespin. You can get the config and color scheme [here.]("http://lyricsdownloader.googlecode.com/files/theme.tar.bz2") The plasma theme is Solid with task items from Aya. The fonts are Segoe with Y2K Neophyte used for the clock. The icons are [Oxygen Refit Black]("http://www.kde-look.org/content/show.php/Oxygen+Refit+Black?content=89298"). I've attached a screenshot of the settings needed to get look of the window decorations. The now playing in the panel is [Playwolf]("http://www.kde-look.org/content/show.php/PlayWolf?content=93882"). The widget on the desktop is a superkaramba theme. I have no plans to distribute it because I don't have copyright on all the images involved.

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2009-05-12

### Post by chucky chuckaluck on 2009-05-12
> **.Maleficus. said:**
> KDE gurus?  Could someone explain to me how to make my GTK apps look like KDE?  I've installed gtk-qt-engine but in the Arch wiki they say to use kcontrol, which doesn't appear to be in KDE 4.x.  Halp?

uninstall gtk-qt-engine and install qtcurve-gtk2 instead. then, go to whichever app you're using to control your gtk themes and select qtcurve and it will follow the kde theme. (edit .gtkrc-2.0 file if you don't have something like lxappearance).

### Post by pt123 on 2009-05-12

### Post by Islington on 2009-05-12
> **pt123 said:**
> How did you get the menu to be semi-transparent like that.

You have to do two things. fire up compiz settings manager:

Turn on the opacity,brightness and saturation plugin.
Create a new entry. 
Set the opacity to 75.
I have this for the Windows value:
```
(type=Menu | PopupMenu | DropdownMenu | Dialog | ModalDialog | Tooltip| Notification| Utility)
``` 
If you want just the menus to be transparent, get rid of ```
Dialog | ModalDialog | Tooltip| Notification| Utility
```


Now to make sure that the menu's are still readable, turn on the blur windows plugin.
Put ```
any
``` in the Alpha blur windows input box. (This means that anywhere there is opacity, the back ground will be blurred.)
Blur Filter : mipmap
MipMap LOD : 2.5


There you are mate.

---

### Post by Vexed Arcanist on 2009-05-13
> **gymophett said:**
> How do I make my Conky like that?! Thats awesome!

[Go here and get Museo 500 font for free.](http://new.myfonts.com/fonts/exljbris/museo/)

[Go here and get Yanone Kaffeesatz for free.](http://www.dafont.com/search.php?psize=m&q=Yanone+Kaffeesatz)

Copy and paste the following in to a conky file,  Now, if you aren't using a 1920x1080 display, you are gonna have to mess with the voffsets, font sizes and offsets of the clock to get it scaled to your display size.

```
background yes
use_xft yes
xftfont Yanone Kaffeesatz:size=16
xftalpha 1
update_interval 1.0
total_run_times 0
own_window yes
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_type desktop
own_window_hints undecorated,below,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager
double_buffer yes
minimum_size 280 200
maximum_width 320
draw_shades no
draw_outline no
draw_borders no
draw_graph_borders no
default_color 122C3D
default_shade_color black
default_outline_color white
alignment top_right
gap_x 22
gap_y 12
no_buffers yes
uppercase no
cpu_avg_samples 2
override_utf8_locale no

TEXT

${goto 30}${font Yanone Kaffeesatz:size=96}${time %H}${voffset -48}${font Yanone Kaffeesatz:bold:size=38}${time :%M}${voffset -18}${font Yanone Kaffeesatz:bold:size=18}${time %S}       

${goto 150}${voffset -10}${font Yanone Kaffeesatz:size=18}${time %A}      
${goto 150}${voffset -4}${time %d %B %Y}  

$mixerbar

${font Museo 500:size=14}${voffset -14}Uptime:$alignr$uptime
CPU1:$alignr${cpu cpu1}%
CPU2:$alignr${cpu cpu2}%
Swap usage:$alignr$swap/$swapmax
RAM:$alignr$mem/$memmax
Ubuntu:  $alignr${fs_used /}/${fs_size /}
Win 7:  $alignr${fs_used /media/sda2}/${fs_size /media/sda2}

```

Now take the following as personal opinion chaps, but kubuntu felt really clunky, say compared to Chakra(KDE mod) or opensuse. I tried only doing Kubuntu for like 8 months or so, and over time the irritations grew. It isnt as smooth or intuitive as gnome yet. Take activities, only in svn is there an easy way to make activities unique to virtual desktop. why wasnt this done earlier/ in the original plan? Its small things like that bothered me. Also kwin blew hardcore in terms of rendering speed when compared to compiz. Ah well, maybe 4.3 will iron out these things..

/rant

### Post by Giant Speck on 2009-05-15
> **RiceMonster said:**
> Nice google theme. Is that done with stylish?

Yep.  It's a userstyle called "Dark Gray Google."  I just tweaked the background a little bit.

```
/*
 * Google Search - Dark Gray Theme
 *
 * Author     : QuestionMarkFTW
 * Updated     : August 30, 2008
 * Description     : Modifies the colors, logos, and a few other images on Google Web Search (http://www.google.ca/ or http://www.google.com/) and Google Image Search (http://images.google.ca/ or http://images.google.com/)
 * Usage           : Use with the Stylish Firefox extension (http://userstyles.org/) or copy to your Firefox userContent.css file
 * Thanks to       : valacar for original coding
 */

@namespace url(http://www.w3.org/1999/xhtml);

@-moz-document url(http://www.google.com/),
               url-prefix(http://www.google.com/webhp),
               url-prefix(http://www.google.com/search?),
               url-prefix(http://www.google.com/advanced_search),
               url-prefix(http://www.google.com/preferences),
               url-prefix(http://www.google.com/language_tools),
               url-prefix(http://images.google.com/webhp),
               url(http://www.google.com/intl/en/),
               url(http://www.google.com/intl/en/options/),
               url-prefix(http://www.google.com/movies),
               url-prefix(http://blogsearch.google.com),
               url-prefix(http://www.google.com/custom?) {

body {
  background: #363330 url("data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAENCAYAAADOoA9GAAAABGdBTUEAAK/INwWK6QAAABl0RVh0U29mdHdhcmUAQWRvYmUgSW1hZ2VSZWFkeXHJZTwAAABZSURBVHjaYmBgYPjPACP+MYFIEPEflfUflwQRSojgUiyGX4IkJTTRi5P4R39T/tFByT8qa6OJof8GPJgGPjHQI/FTki+pWFCQXlQhsZiBmBFMwLlgwAgQYAAYPe0bQ81rlgAAAABJRU5ErkJggg==") top left repeat-x !important;
  color: #fff !important;
}

/* defaults for all links */
a:link, a:visited, .link, a font[color] { color: #ccc !important; }
a:active, .link:active, a:active font[color] { color: #fff !important; }

/* disable dashed outline on focused elements */
:focus { outline: none; }

/* Main text color */
div, td, font[color="#000000"] { color: #fff !important; }

/* Text link color */
.a, .g font[color="#008000"], cite, .cite, .cite:link, .a { color: #6e6e6e !important; }

font[color="#008000"] { color: #6e6e6e !important; }

/* Secondary link color */
.flc, a.fl, .fl2, .fl2:visited, .bl a, .f + a, .f .w { color: #7b7b7b !important; }

/* File type (ex: [PDF]) next to link */
.g .w { color: #ff6 !important; }

/* Alt text color */
.f, font[color="#666666"], font[color="#6f6f6f"], font[color="#555555"], font[color="#0000ff"] { color: #ffd !important; }

/* Notification message text color */
font.p:not([size="-1"]) { color: #a4ff53 !important; }

/* fix for google suggest */
.aAutoComplete .cAutoComplete, .google-ac-a .google-ac-c, .gac_a > .gac_c { color: #000 !important; }
.aAutoComplete .dAutoComplete, .google-ac-a .google-ac-d, .gac_a > .gac_d { color: green !important; }

  background-color: #3f3f3f !important;
}

And for the logo:

```
/*
 * Google Web Search - gray logo replacement
 *
 * Author      : Valacar
 * Updated     : August 10th, 2008
 * Website     : http://www.valacar.com/userstyles/
 * Description : Replaces the Google Web Search logo with a grayscale version (works best with dark backgrounds)
 *               IMPORTANT: This is the logo images ONLY!
 * Required    : "Google Web Search - dark gray redesign (vC)" should be installed as well.  You can find it on
 *               http://userstyles.org/style/show/1693 or on my web site (listed above).
 * Usage       : Use with Stylish Firefox extension (http://userstyles.org/) or copy to your Firefox userContent.css file
 */

### Post by racerraul on 2009-05-18
> **Dawei87 said:**
> thats pretty slick! would you mind sharing your conky with me?

.conkyrc
```
background yes
use_xft yes
xftalpha 0.1
update_interval 3.0
total_run_times 0
own_window yes
own_window_type normal
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_hints undecorated,below,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager
double_buffer yes
minimum_size 225 5
maximum_width 300
draw_shades no
draw_outline no
draw_borders no
draw_graph_borders no
default_color white
default_shade_color red
default_outline_color green
alignment top_right
gap_x 25
gap_y 45
no_buffers yes
uppercase no
cpu_avg_samples 2
net_avg_samples 1
override_utf8_locale yes
use_spacer right
max_specials 1024
max_user_text 10000
text_buffer_size 1024


TEXT
${font Starcraft:size=12}${color #B787C6}OpenGEU 8.10 Luna Serena ${color LightGray}${hr 2}
${font Newtext Rg BT:size=10}${color LightGray}Ubuntu ${alignr}Enlightenment DR17
$sysname $kernel $alignr $machine
${font Newtext Rg BT:size=10}${color LightGray}System Temperature${alignr}${execi 2 cat /sys/bus/pci/drivers/k8temp/000*/temp1_input | cut -c1,2}°C

${font Starcraft:size=12}${color #B787C6}PROCESSORS ${color LightGray}${hr 2}
${font Newtext Rg BT:size=10}${color LightGray}AMD Athlon 64 X2 6000+ $alignr${freq_g cpu0}Ghz
CPU: 1  ${color red}${cpubar cpu1}
${font Newtext Rg BT:size=10}${color LightGray}AMD Athlon 64 X2 6000+ $alignr${freq_g cpu0}Ghz
CPU: 2  ${color red}${cpubar cpu2}

${font Starcraft:size=12}${color #B787C6}MEMORY ${color LightGray}${hr 2}
${font Newtext Rg BT:size=10}${color LightGray}$alignc $mem / $memmax $alignr $memperc%
${color Yellow}$membar

${font Starcraft:size=12}${color #B787C6}DRIVE SPACE ${color LightGray}${hr 2}
${font Newtext Rg BT:size=10}${color LightGray}/home $alignc ${fs_used /home} / ${fs_size /home} $alignr ${fs_free_perc /home}%
${color Tan}${fs_bar /home}
${color LightGray}/Storage $alignc ${fs_used /home/racerraul/Storage} / ${fs_size /home/racerraul/Storage} $alignr ${fs_free_perc /home/racerraul/Storage}%
${color Tan}${fs_bar /home/racerraul/Storage}

${font Starcraft:size=12}${color #B787C6}PROCESSES ${color LightGray}${hr 2}
${font Newtext Rg BT:size=10}${color LightGray}$running_processes Running $alignr $processes Sleeping

Top Processes
${hr 1}
CPU $alignr CPU%   MEM%

${top name 1}$alignr${top cpu 1}     ${top mem 1}
${top name 2}$alignr${top cpu 2}     ${top mem 2}
${top name 3}$alignr${top cpu 2}     ${top mem 3}

MEM $alignr CPU%   MEM%

${top_mem name 1}$alignr${top_mem cpu 1}     ${top_mem mem 1}
${top_mem name 2}$alignr${top_mem cpu 2}     ${top_mem mem 2}
${top_mem name 3}$alignr${top_mem cpu 3}     ${top_mem mem 3}

${font Starcraft:size=12}${color #B787C6}WEATHER ${color LightGray}${hr 2}

${font Newtext Rg BT:size=10}${color LightGray}Cleveland, TN${goto 140}${voffset -19}${color Tan}${font ConkyWeather:size=26}${execi 1800 conkyForecast --location=USTN0084 --datatype=WF}${font}${color} ${voffset -19}${font Newtext Rg BT:size=16}${color LightGray}${execi 1800 conkyForecast --imperial --location=USTN0084 --datatype=HT}
${voffset 5}${font Newtext Rg BT:size=10}${color LightGray}Current Conditions:  ${color Tan}${execi 1800 conkyForecast --location=USTN0084 --datatype=CC}${color}   
${color LightGray}Humidity:  ${color Tan}${execi 1800 conkyForecast --location=USTN0084 --datatype=HM}${color}
${color LightGray}Rain Chance:  ${color Tan}${execi 1800 conkyForecast --location=USTN0084 --startday=0 --datatype=PC}${color}
${color LightGray}Winds:  ${color Tan}${execi 1800 conkyForecast --location=USTN0084 --datatype=WD}${color}
${color LightGray}Moon Phase:  ${color Tan}${execi 1800 conkyForecast --location=USTN0084 --datatype=MP}    ${voffset -22}${font Moon Phases:size=26}${color TAN}${execi 1800 conkyForecast --location=USTN0084 --datatype=MF}${font}
${voffset -2}${font Newtext Rg BT:size=10}${color LightGray}Sunrise:  ${color Tan}${execi 1800 conkyForecast --location=USTN0084 --datatype=SR}${color} / Sunset:  ${color Tan}${execi 1800 conkyForecast --location=USTN0084 --datatype=SS}
${font Newtext Rg BT:size=10}${color LightGray}${hr 1}
${voffset -6}${alignc} 5 Day Forecast
${voffset -9}${hr 1}
${execpi 1800 conkyForecast --location=USTN0084 --template=/home/racerraul/.conkyweather.template}
${font Starcraft:size=12}${color #B787C6}TIME & DATE ${color LightGray}${hr 2}

${voffset -10}${color LightGray} ${font Vibrocentric:size=20}$alignc${time %H:%M}
${voffset -10}${font Vibrocentric:bold:size=10}$alignc${time %b. %d %Y}
${font Vibrocentric:bold:size=8}$alignc${time %A}
```

.conkyweather.template

${color Tan}${font ConkyWeather:size=26}[--datatype=WF --startday=0]${goto 65}[--datatype=WF --startday=1]${goto 130}[--datatype=WF --startday=2]${goto 195}[--datatype=WF --startday=3]${goto 260}[--datatype=WF --startday=4]${font}${color}
${color LightGray}${font Newtext Rg BT:size=10}[--datatype=DW --shortweekday --startday=0]${goto 65}[--datatype=DW --shortweekday --startday=1]${goto 130}[--datatype=DW --shortweekday --startday=2]${goto 195}[--datatype=DW --shortweekday --startday=3]${goto 260}[--datatype=DW --shortweekday --startday=4]${color}
${color Red}[--datatype=HT --imperial --startday=0]${goto 65}[--datatype=HT --imperial --startday=1]${goto 130}[--datatype=HT --imperial --startday=2]${goto 195}[--datatype=HT --imperial --startday=3]${goto 260}[--datatype=HT --imperial --startday=4]${color}
${color Blue}[--datatype=LT --imperial --startday=0]${goto 65}[--datatype=LT --imperial --startday=1]${goto 130}[--datatype=LT --imperial --startday=2]${goto 195}[--datatype=LT --imperial --startday=3]${goto 260}[--datatype=LT --imperial --startday=4]${color}
${color LightBlue}[--datatype=PC --imperial --startday=0]${goto 65}[--datatype=PC --imperial --startday=1]${goto 130}[--datatype=PC --imperial --startday=2]${goto 195}[--datatype=PC --imperial --startday=3]${goto 260}[--datatype=PC --imperial --startday=4]${color}
```

### Post by sertse on 2009-05-18
Responding to a PM request

[QUOTE=pp7]Hi, what is the system tray program that you are using in this screenshot?: [http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=7037565&postcount=459](http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=7037565&postcount=459)

Thanks,[/QUOTE]

Firstly an updated screenshot,  though regulars of this threads will have seen it

It is docker, available in the repos. Works best with fluxbox (which is what I'm using) and openbox, where it'll allow you to control where it is positioned. If it doesn't work try stalonetray or trayer. They must more configurable options I think, at least not relying on the WM for positioning, but I prefer docker where it works :) 

Soeaking of system trays... subtle reminder for RiceMonster to respond to my earlier post when he gets on.

### Post by ubuntu-freak on 2009-05-18
Mine is fairly simple, but took a while to get just how I want it. The system monitor to the right is SysMonitor Plus and is available for download [here](http://www.compiz-themes.org/content/show.php?content=100042&forumpage=2&PHPSESSID=84ba9e4cead1d2d6c525068aca4d). To use that particular app, you need to install Screenlets:

**sudo apt-get install screenlets**

Next, launch Screenlets in "Applications > Accessories > Screenlets" and install SysMonitor Plus with the "Install" option. Once you've finished personalising SysMonitor Plus, restart it before powering down - or your changes may not be saved. To get your local weather showing, go to weather.com and search for your country and town, then copy the 8 digit code from the address bar, right-click on SysMonitor Plus on your desktop, navigate to "Properties > Options > Weather", then replace the zip code there with the weather.com code for where you live.

The transparent terminal on my desktop is Tilda and the cursor theme is ComixCursors:

**sudo apt-get install comixcursors tilda**

For some reason, Tilda only becomes 90% transparent for me, despite how it looks on my desktop, which could be related to the current Jaunty vs Intel issues. I used colour trickery to make it appear transparent. If you have the same problem as me, report a bug, then play with the terminal background colour in Tilda's preferences until it appears transparent.

If you want system icons to show on your desktop and don't know how to do it, execute the following command:

**gksudo gconf-editor**

Next, navigate to "apps > nautilus > desktop" and tick the relevant boxes. You can also right-click on each one to make the setting default for all users. Finally, reboot/log out so the icons appear on your desktop.

Peace.

---

### Post by mrdiego on 2009-05-19
>  Erectus is an incredible project! I kinda wish they would release a new version soon, as it embodies the Ubuntu spirit better than gnome-human which is distro-agnostic by design. BTW is there a link to that "Wasp" theme? It looks really smooth and soothing.

Edit: How do you get nautilus sidebar icons to be 24px? It looks much better than the default config.

The Wasp-theme is here: [http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Wasp?content=104167](http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Wasp?content=104167)

For some bugs in FF I am using the alternate. The opacity-script by default I would let it. For my part I used this vanilla-script for some metacity-mods ...

Nautilus was modified and compiled for geting it this kind. Here is a link for the workaround: [http://www.virtualpixel.de/linux/nautilus-sidebar-modding](http://www.virtualpixel.de/linux/nautilus-sidebar-modding)

About Erectus-Human:

Till now it isn't complete. But I think 1.0 will be quite good. I am nearly sure I will make again some mods for my own gust with it. Gtk-media form the original Gnome-Theme is more what I like. The volumes-icons in Human (22x22) too. Ohh start-here of course ... :D The Ubuntu-Logo is naturally a must for me. ;)

Gnome-Colors:

Perfect work [icons] - perfect build (naming, sym-links, etc.) ... simply the most mature icon-set I know for Gnome. Good to have it. ;)

Oliver

### Post by armageddon08 on 2009-05-20
> **Daisuke_Aramaki said:**
> you can probably turn off the bold switch in your Xdefaults, since with pcf fonts like terminus, montecarlo, profont, proggy family, and artwiz, the bold ones would look hideous. kind of distracting when spending a lot of time on vim, coding, for example. or may be you intended that way?

Can you tell me how to install .pcf fonts(esp. artwiz fonts) in jaunty? I tried the usual way of placing the files under /usr/share/fonts, but it does not show up in the font-selection menu in gnome-appearance properties.

---

### Post by dbbolton on 2009-05-20
> **armageddon08 said:**
> Can you tell me how to install .pcf fonts(esp. artwiz fonts) in jaunty? I tried the usual way of placing the files under /usr/share/fonts, but it does not show up in the font-selection menu in gnome-appearance properties.
In Jaunty you have to remove this file first: '/etc/fonts/conf.d/70-no-bitmaps.conf'

confer [http://demonic.cc/?p=21](http://demonic.cc/?p=21)

### Post by raul_ on 2009-05-21
> **open_coder said:**
> I am running the 4.3 beta and I haven't been able to figure out the whole make the dashboard separate from the desktop thing. Do you think maybe you could help me out?

Alex

Sure.
Click the cashew and zoom out.
Now you'll have a bunch of new options, including "configure Plasma".
Click on it and then "Separate dashboard from desktop".
After that you just bring the dashboard up and add widgets to it. Maybe a little buggy on the beta, though.

### Post by MurkMenthaa on 2009-05-21
> **Marlonsm said:**
> How can I do that transparent menus?
Also, does it work for tooltips too?


Compiz settinngs > Opacity, Brightness plugin > Window Specific Settings > New > add "(type=Menu | PopupMenu | DropdownMenu)" in Windows textbox & set transparency to 70-80.

---

### Post by zurack on 2009-05-21
> **Vexed Arcanist said:**
> Folder view is a widget, right click desktop and add widget.

I have seen some users have what looks like the whole desktop as a folder view so that icons can be placed like in kde3/Gnome (not that I have icons on the desktop)

> **chucky chuckaluck said:**
> which plasma theme is that?

It's Slim Glow with Glassified panel (custom)

---

### Post by eightmillion on 2009-05-21
> **zurack said:**
> I have seen some users have what looks like the whole desktop as a folder view so that icons can be placed like in kde3/Gnome (not that I have icons on the desktop)



It's Slim Glow with Glassified panel (custom)

Right click on your desktop and choose "Appearance Settings". At the very top of the dialog, there's a listbox to choose the desktop type. Change that to folderview.

---

### Post by armageddon08 on 2009-05-21
> **zurack said:**
> I have seen some users have what looks like the whole desktop as a folder view so that icons can be placed like in kde3/Gnome (not that I have icons on the desktop)



It's Slim Glow with Glassified panel (custom)

Right Click on the desktop. Select Appearance Properties; select folder-view from desktop containment.
[EDIT]: Eightmillion got first.

### Post by zurack on 2009-05-21
> **eightmillion said:**
> Right click on your desktop and choose "Appearance Settings". At the very top of the dialog, there's a listbox to choose the desktop type. Change that to folderview.


> **armageddon08 said:**
> Right Click on the desktop. Select Appearance Properties; select folder-view from desktop containment.
[EDIT]: Eightmillion got first.


Many thanks. :)

### Post by rjmdomingo2003 on 2009-05-22
> **Vexed Arcanist said:**
> Could I get that conkyrc and tint2rc?

I believe the GTK/OB is Turqouise Grass, a deviation of Hanna's Black Grass.
You're right about the theme. Thanks for pointing that out.

conkyrc:
```
own_window no
own_window_type normal
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_hints undecorate,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager
double_buffer yes
short_units yes
use_xft yes
update_interval 2
draw_shades no
draw_outline no
xftfont AvantGardeLTMedium:bold:pixelsize=16
minimum_size 1280 0
default_color fffefc
alignment top_left
gap_x 15
gap_y 15

TEXT
${font AvantGardeLTMedium:pixelsize=8}${execi 1800 python ~/scripts/conkyForecast.py --location=AEXX0004 --datatype=CC}
${font}${voffset -6}${execi 1800 python ~/scripts/conkyForecast.py --location=AEXX0004 --datatype=HT}${font AvantGardeLTMedium:bold:pixelsize=8}${color a9a28f}
${voffset -1}${cpugraph cpu1 10,40}
${cpugraph cpu2 10,40}${color}
${offset 12}${voffset -23}${cpu cpu1}%
${offset 12}${cpu cpu2}%
${voffset -2}${font AvantGardeLTMedium:pixelsize=6}${execi 3600 remind '-kecho %s'}
```

tintrc:
```
#---------------------------------------------
# TINT CONFIG FILE
#---------------------------------------------

#---------------------------------------------
# PANEL
#---------------------------------------------
panel_mode = multi_desktop
panel_monitor = 1
panel_position = bottom left
panel_size = 1280 24
panel_margin = 0 0
panel_padding = 10 0
font_shadow = 0

#---------------------------------------------
# PANEL BACKGROUND AND BORDER
#---------------------------------------------
panel_rounded = 0
panel_border_width = 0
panel_background_color = #000000 100
panel_border_color = #ffffff 90

#---------------------------------------------
# TASKS
#---------------------------------------------
task_text_centered = 1
task_width = 110
task_margin = 1
task_padding = 2
task_icon_size = 0
task_font = kroeger 05_55 caps 6
task_font_color = #ffffff 12
task_active_font_color = #61b382 100

#---------------------------------------------
# TASK BACKGROUND AND BORDER
#---------------------------------------------
task_rounded = 1
task_background_color = #6b5d4a 0
task_active_background_color = #222222 0
task_border_width = 0
task_border_color = #ffffff 18
task_active_border_color = #ffffff 70

#---------------------------------------------
# CLOCK
#---------------------------------------------
time1_format = %H:%M
time1_font = HeldustryFTVBasic Regular 10
#time2_format = %d %b. %Y
#time2_font = Myriad Pro Condensed 10
clock_font_color = #ffffff 100

#---------------------------------------------
# MOUSE ACTION ON TASK
#---------------------------------------------
mouse_middle = none
mouse_right = close
mouse_scroll_up = toggle
mouse_scroll_down = iconify
```

### Post by sertse on 2009-05-22
> **SomeGuyDude said:**
> In looking at all my desks over the past four months I've realized something. I'm not changing the setup of my desk in any substantial way, just flipping around GTK/icons/wallpaper. I'm always on Compiz, my panel/conky doesn't change, nothin'. Just new colors.

I needs me some inspiration.

I'm feeling the same. Even worse, it's just wallpapers nowadays. This is especially the case with fluxbox on my netbook. Any fluxbox user user would know the insane effort to create the customised menu, (the autogen debian menu is *not* sane) especially *manually* matching each menu item to an icon. Then there are the custom keybindings etc. Starting all over again from scratch using something requires much effort.

Atm though, I'm continuing to deconstruct what was stock xfce on my desktop. I already replaced the session manager with lxde's. Now I'm looking at replacing xfwm with open/fluxbox and maybe even the panel with tint. xfdesktop is the only component I really need these days, now that xfce 4.6, following freedesktop specs has sane autogenerated menus, and only minor adjustments are needed. Autogenerated menus ftw :)

P.S: Giant Speck. Wow. wow. You reproduced that screenlet with conky...insanely accurately.

### Post by Giant Speck on 2009-05-23
> **Tipped OuT said:**
> Why would you want to disable the text shadow? It's there so you can read the text, no matter what background you have.

But then again, personal preference I guess. :p

There are certain backgrounds where a dark text shadow actually makes it difficult to read the icon text.  Also, if I'm using a neutral background such as a subtle texture or gradient, shadowless icon text looks best.  At least for me.

KDE 3.5.9 allowed me to enable/disable text shadow, change the color of the icon text, and allowed me to adjust the spacing of the windows.  This was probably because the desktop on KDE 3.5.9 wasn't controlled by a file manager.  On Gnome 2.26, the desktop is controlled by Nautilus, so there aren't many options for desktop icons.  You can't change the colors, you can't change the shadows, and the only two icon alignment options are "keep aligned" and "clean up by name."

---

### Post by BwackNinja on 2009-05-24
> **armageddon08 said:**
> Love that set-up. Could you tell me how to get one like that?
First you get so bored that you decide that despite the multitude of desktop widgets available, you have to make your own, so you learn python with cairo and search the internet for how to do exactly what you want to do.

Beyond the desktop widgets, lets see if I can sum up everything I did to my desktop...

I'm using xfce4-panel and transparent images as buttons (they look soooo much smoother than themed buttons) with a gtk theme I hacked together myself out of a few other themes, with almost nothing recognizable left. I modified an emerald theme to match. I used the stylish extension on firefox to make the nice bookmark menus look like menus and also modify how google looks and such. I modified the Eikon icon theme to have dark toolbar stuff from Oxygen Refit 2 Black. I'm using compiz-deskmenu to provide my right-click menu. Wallpaper from interfacelift.

I can upload any part of it on request.

Also - @Tipped OuT: That wallpaper is Awesome.

---

### Post by sertse on 2009-05-25
Fluxbox + Xfdesktop = Perfect. 

This is the merger of the setups I have previously running on my netbook (fluxbox) and desktop (xfce). As said on my last post, creating usable menus is one of the most annonying aspects of a *box WM, while xfwm has less customisability in window control than the boxes. I choose fluxbox mainly because it includes a panel, allowing me to remove xfce-panel as well, saving a bit more memory.

### Post by londonali1010 on 2009-05-25
Geeeeez. You guys are killin' me. Since I got hooked on this thread, I've been tinkering pretty much solidly!

Here's my latest effort, which I think I'll keep for a while. It's pretty much entirely stolen/modified from bits of other peoples' desktops, so I'll give credit where it's due.

[ATTACH]115100[/ATTACH][ATTACH]115101[/ATTACH]

* Wallpaper is from Zixpk.com ([http://www.zixpk.com/2008/09/hd-wallpaper-aker.html]("http://www.zixpk.com/2008/09/hd-wallpaper-aker.html")), thanks to someone earlier on this thread for pointing me in the right direction
* GTK theme is dust sand
* Emerald theme is my own, modified from White Mod ([http://www.gnome-look.org]("http://www.gnome-look.org")): changed engine, titlebar alignment, border/text sizes (to fit my tiny screen!)
* Panel is normal gnome-panel, but set to match the window borders
* Dock is AWN, with my own theme (just default with modified colours, etc.)

I'm also running Compiz with just a teensy bit of transparency on the windows, and yes, before you say, it, I know I should be using alpha blur! However, I've tried using blur twice now, and both times it's turned my screen into a big black nothing and I've had to boot to recovery mode to sort it out (ouch!).

By the way, would someone PLEASE convince me it's a bad idea to try KDE? Because all the screenies here are gorgeous, and ME WANT, but I don't need anything else to install on my poor little netbook!

---

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2009-05-26
> **londonali1010 said:**
> @raul_, @perfectska04:-

KDE isn't a bad idea, but me putting more stuff on my netbook should be! I've only got an 8GB SSD, which I'm rapidly filling up! I've got just over 1GB left. Would be okay, because there's an expansion slot for 2 SD cards, but one doesn't work in Jaunty (yet!), and I need the other one hot-pluggable, so I can't use a fixed expansion yet.

Since I've already got a bunch of stuff installed for Gnome, if I also install KDE and more associated stuff, how much of my drive will it eat?!

PS. Thanks, guys. All this prettification is helping me on my mission to convert everyone I know to Linux :)
This is where the mini.iso and --no-install-recommends argument comes in handy when apt-get/aptitude installing stuff. 

Failing that, if you open up synaptic and just list all the stuff that's installed, you should be able to remove several hundred packages without losing any functionality (for example, you've no doubt got xorg video drivers installed for about 25 different cards you don't have). Removing old kernels frees up a lot of space, too.

Running:

sudo aptitude clean

Also ought to help.

[img]http://img8.imageshack.us/img8/492/screenshotcos.png[/img]


Just be careful when uninstalling stuff: if synaptic informs you that 20 other packages need to be removed as well and those packages happen to include stuff like Dbus, Gdm, Gnome-whatever, Hal, etc, *click cancel.*

---

KDE isn't a bad idea, but me putting more stuff on my netbook should be! I've only got an 8GB SSD, which I'm rapidly filling up! I've got just over 1GB left. Since I've already got a bunch of stuff installed for Gnome, if I also install KDE and more associated stuff, how much of my drive will it eat?!

PS. Thanks, guys. All this prettification is helping me on my mission to convert everyone I know to Linux :)

you could do a kdebase installation instead of all of kde. kdebase comes with dolphin, konqueror, konsole and the like. then, you can add things that you need/want. depending on what you want, it could cut down on the space you'd use by as much as half.

### Post by Daisuke_Aramaki on 2009-05-26
> **Tipped OuT said:**
> What's that? Please explain, I have the same theme as him as well.

[[img]http://g.imagehost.org/t/0179/77783-2.jpg[/img]](http://g.imagehost.org/view/0179/77783-2)

see the difference between the two pictures. look at the inactive buttons. pixbuf engine by default renders them ugly like in picture two. but with the patched engine, you can make them transparent.

Get the patched engine [here]("http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/gtk2-engine-pixbuf+(Patched)?content=77783")

---

### Post by Vexed Arcanist on 2009-05-27
> **gymophett said:**
> I am using Crunchbang! I love it. :) Read my signature.

@Chucky Chuckaluck..
How do you manage to have so many window managers all the time?! You always switch. :P

Your using CrunchBang has nothing to do with you misqualifying it as simply Ubuntu with Openbox.  Anyone with Ubuntu can add openbox and it won't be the same speedy, snappy CrunchBang.  There is quite a difference, as you would know had you tried Ubuntu with Openbox first.  Much of the gnome apps, daemons, etc., are intentionally removed and replaced with GTK equivalents or other speedier replacements.

---

### Post by Sand &amp; Mercury on 2009-05-27
> **Hund said:**
> ISP caps? Whats that?
Limits to how much you can download/upload in a month; if you go over the cap, they'll either start charging you extra or choke your internet speed to usually something like 64kbps (ie. the bandwidth you'd get out of some cups and string). It's very popular among ISPs in Australia where internet services are about six or seven years behind the times.

---

### Post by Hund on 2009-05-27
> **Sand & Mercury said:**
> Limits to how much you can download/upload in a month; if you go over the cap, they'll either start charging you extra or choke your internet speed to usually something like 64kbps (ie. the bandwidth you'd get out of some cups and string). It's very popular among ISPs in Australia where internet services are about six or seven years behind the times.

Ah, thx. :)

Sounds like a stupid idea.

### Post by dbbolton on 2009-05-27
> **chucky chuckaluck said:**
> which theme is that?

edit: got it! openbox should give you some kind of award for best themes.

Thanks man. Actually I felt surprisingly rewarded when I found out that a couple things I submitted to box-look wound up in the openbox-themes debian package ;)


> **sertse said:**
> 25mb on openbox? Good job, good job.

I guess the Arch developers are doing the good job. Here is Debian (but also pypanel, which might use 10 MB) running on the same computer:

[[IMG]http://i103.photobucket.com/albums/m128/envyouraudience/sshot/th_2009-03-19-151728_1024x768_scrot.png[/IMG]]("http://s103.photobucket.com/albums/m128/envyouraudience/sshot/?action=view&current=2009-03-19-151728_1024x768_scrot.png")

I put the output of free on the Arch system below.

> **etnlIcarus said:**
> I'm not sure how memory usage on /proc/meminfo is calculated but it's not the same as, say, free -m, minus buffers (how most apps count memory usage).

His free -m output is probably more around the 70-90mb mark.

This is how:  [http://www.redhat.com/docs/manuals/enterprise/RHEL-4-Manual/en-US/Reference_Guide/s2-proc-meminfo.html](http://www.redhat.com/docs/manuals/enterprise/RHEL-4-Manual/en-US/Reference_Guide/s2-proc-meminfo.html)

> 
Active &#8212; The total amount of buffer or page cache memory, in kilobytes, that is in active use. This is memory that has been recently used and is usually not reclaimed for other purposes. 
Just for kicks I added 'free -m >& free_m.log' to my austostart.sh (a file that is executed by openbox when openbox-session is executed, which is in my .xinitrc) and here it is:

```

             total       used       free     shared    buffers     cached
Mem:           122         47         74          0          4         24
-/+ buffers/cache:         17        104
Swap:          128          0        128

```For even more kicks I tried it with no X:
```

             total       used       free     shared    buffers     cached
Mem:           122         34         87          0          4         16
-/+ buffers/cache:         13        108
Swap:          128          0        128

```

> **dbbolton said:**
> This is how:  [http://www.redhat.com/docs/manuals/enterprise/RHEL-4-Manual/en-US/Reference_Guide/s2-proc-meminfo.html](http://www.redhat.com/docs/manuals/enterprise/RHEL-4-Manual/en-US/Reference_Guide/s2-proc-meminfo.html)

Just for kicks I added 'free -m >& free_m.log' to my austostart.sh (a file that is executed by openbox when openbox-session is executed, which is in my .xinitrc) and here it is:

```

             total       used       free     shared    buffers     cached
Mem:           122         47         74          0          4         24
-/+ buffers/cache:         17        104
Swap:          128          0        128

```For even more kicks I tried it with no X:
```

             total       used       free     shared    buffers     cached
Mem:           122         34         87          0          4         16
-/+ buffers/cache:         13        108
Swap:          128          0        128

```13mb? I've only ever seen results like that running in a VM. You must be running some kind of ancient and highly generic system.

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2009-05-29
> **xX-Felipao-Xx said:**
> Thanks, and I don't like its likeness with Vista borders neither. I've been searching borders for a long while but nothing interesting...

any recommendation? (the same if its emerald or metacity)I haven't used Metacity for at least 2 years and as for emerald, I gave up looking for decent emerald themes a long time ago and just started making my own. I recommend playing around with the emerald theme manager. See what you can come up with. If you're more comfortable with pixmap editing, just create a template in the Gimp and chop it up for use with emerald's pixmap engine.

This is what I've built my current xfwm and emerald themes from, for example:

[img]http://img132.imageshack.us/img132/5228/slicktemp3.jpg[/img]

(actual size)

---

### Post by Vexed Arcanist on 2009-05-29
> **burvowski said:**
> any chance you could paste your conky config? (and maybe scripts too?)

also...what music player is that? is it hard to get it configured to look like that? looks like it would work great on my eee pc

Music player is mocp, theme is transparent-background.  From a terminal you would simply call the music player [HTML]mocp -T transparent-theme[/HTML].

The fonts I use are scaled large since this is displayed on a 42" HD TV, you will have to change font sizes and possibly the goto and offset information in the conky script.  You will also need to edit or remove the weather section; I used [this thread](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=1156383&highlight=conky+weather) when setting up the weather info.

The panel I use is tint2.

.conkyrc

```
background yes
use_xft yes
xftfont Yanone Kaffeesatz:size=16
xftalpha 1
update_interval 1.0
total_run_times 0
own_window yes
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_type desktop
own_window_hints undecorated,below,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager
double_buffer yes
minimum_size 280 200
maximum_width 320
draw_shades no
draw_outline no
draw_borders no
draw_graph_borders no
default_color ededed #122C3D
default_shade_color black
default_outline_color white
alignment top_right
gap_x 22
gap_y 12
no_buffers yes
uppercase no
cpu_avg_samples 2
override_utf8_locale no
TEXT
${goto 50}${font Yanone Kaffeesatz:size=96}${time %H}${voffset -48}${font Yanone Kaffeesatz:bold:size=38}${time :%M}${voffset -18}${font Yanone Kaffeesatz:bold:size=18}${time %S}       

${goto 170}${voffset -10}${font Yanone Kaffeesatz:size=18}${time %A}      
${goto 170}${voffset -4}${time %d %B %Y}  

$mixerbar

${voffset -14}Uptime:$alignr$uptime
RAM:$alignr$mem/$memmax
Swap usage:$alignr$swap/$swapmax
Disk usage:$alignr${fs_used /}/${fs_size /}
Processor #1:$alignr${cpu cpu1}%
Processor #2:$alignr${cpu cpu2}% 

${color}${font Yanone Kaffeesatz:size=16}LOCAL WEATHER ${hr 2}$color${execi 600 sh /home/tony/bin/weather_script.sh}

${font ConkyWeather:size=28}${execi 600  sed -n '4p' /home/tony/bin/weather1}${font} ${voffset -20}${execi 600 sed -n '1p' /home/tony/bin/weather1}

${rss http://rss.accuweather.com/rss/liveweather_rss.asp?locCode=35040&metric= 10 item_title 1}
${font ConkyWeather:size=28}${execi 600  sed -n '5p' /home/tony/bin/weather1}${font} ${voffset -20}${execi 600 sed -n '2p' /home/tony/bin/weather1}

${rss http://rss.accuweather.com/rss/liveweather_rss.asp?locCode=35040&metric= 10 item_title 2}
${font ConkyWeather:size=28}${execi 600  sed -n '6p' /home/tony/bin/weather1}${font} ${voffset -20}${execi 600 sed -n '3p' /home/tony/bin/weather1}

TOP PROCESSES ${hr 2}

NAME $alignr PID    CPU
${top name 1} $alignr ${top pid 1} ${top cpu 1}
${top name 2} $alignr ${top pid 2} ${top cpu 2}
${top name 3} $alignr ${top pid 3} ${top cpu 3}
${top name 4} $alignr ${top pid 4} ${top cpu 4}
${top name 5} $alignr ${top pid 5} ${top cpu 5}
${top name 6} $alignr ${top pid 6} ${top cpu 6}
${top name 7} $alignr ${top pid 7} ${top cpu 7}
${top name 8} $alignr ${top pid 8} ${top cpu 8}

NOW PLAYING ${hr 2}

$alignc${exec mocp -Q %artist} ${exec mocp -Q %song}
```

tint2rc

```
#---------------------------------------------
# TINT2 CONFIG FILE
#---------------------------------------------

#---------------------------------------------
# BACKGROUND AND BORDER
#---------------------------------------------
rounded = 14
border_width = 2
background_color = #000000 100
border_color = #f6f6f6 100

rounded = 9
border_width = 2
background_color = #000000 100
border_color = #f6f6f6 100

rounded = 9
border_width = 2
background_color = #000000 100
border_color = #f6f6f6 60

#---------------------------------------------
# PANEL
#---------------------------------------------
panel_monitor = all
panel_position = bottom center
panel_size = 82% 36
panel_margin = 0 32
panel_padding = 7 0
font_shadow = 0
panel_background_id = 1

#---------------------------------------------
# TASKBAR
#---------------------------------------------
taskbar_mode = single_monitor
taskbar_padding = 2 3 2
taskbar_background_id = 0

#---------------------------------------------
# TASKS
#---------------------------------------------
task_icon = 0
task_text = 1
task_width = 140
task_centered = 1
task_padding = 6 3
task_font = Yanone Kaffeesatz 16
task_font_color = #f6f6f6 60
task_active_font_color = #f6f6f6 100
task_background_id = 3
task_active_background_id = 2

#---------------------------------------------
# SYSTRAYBAR
#---------------------------------------------
systray_padding = 0 4 5
systray_background_id = 0

#---------------------------------------------
# CLOCK
#---------------------------------------------
#time1_format = %H:%M
#time1_font = sans 8
#time2_format = %A %d %B
#time2_font = sans 6
#clock_font_color = #f6f6f6 76
#clock_padding = 1 0
#clock_background_id = 0

#---------------------------------------------
# MOUSE ACTION ON TASK
#---------------------------------------------
mouse_middle = none
mouse_right = close
mouse_scroll_up = toggle
mouse_scroll_down = iconify


```

### Post by gymophett on 2009-05-30
> **Viva said:**
> Details please..

Sure thing. It did not all come in one theme pack though. So here we go.

Wallpaper: [http://www.zixpk.com/2008/07/hd-wallpaper-digilove-carbon.html](http://www.zixpk.com/2008/07/hd-wallpaper-digilove-carbon.html)
GTK theme 1 (controls): [http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/BSM+Suite?content=96710](http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/BSM+Suite?content=96710)

Use the BSM silver. Go to customize and use BSM Silver for controls. (Make sure it is NOT BSM flat)

GTK theme 2: [http://www.elementary-project.com/downloads.html](http://www.elementary-project.com/downloads.html)
Download the Window Theme.
Once Download, unzip the folder and install the .deb file.
Now, under customization use eGTK for the window theme.

Icons: [http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/MacUltimate+Leopard?content=82844](http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/MacUltimate+Leopard?content=82844)

Fonts: [http://www.ubuntu-inside.me/2009/02/installing-mac-fonts-on-ubuntu.html](http://www.ubuntu-inside.me/2009/02/installing-mac-fonts-on-ubuntu.html)

Use his font setup too.
Then use DMZ (Black) pointer.
Should be all done then. :D

---

### Post by Giant Speck on 2009-05-30
This new theme is really growing on me.  And the more I look at it, the more I have to agree that it looks like dark chocolate.  It was originally supposed to be a "no sugar, no cream" version of Macchiato that I was going to call "Espresso."

I did some experimenting with combining a couple wallpapers (KDE's default "Air" wallpaper and a wallpaper from Alexander_GG's "Colored Backgrounds" set).

I also installed the Breath icon set.  This is the first time I've installed a new icon set since December 2008, when I started using Eikon.

EDIT:  Also, is there anyway to disable scrollbars in Nautilus like you can in gnome-terminal?

### Post by eightmillion on 2009-05-31
> **savagenator said:**
> [[IMG]http://img188.imageshack.us/img188/559/screenshotblue.th.png[/IMG]](http://img188.imageshack.us/my.php?image=screenshotblue.png)

This is mine. I got really frustrated that There is a bar on the BOTTOM of my screen taking up valuable vertical space, so I moved it. Stasks (yes I know, windows 7...) is really useful, unfortunately it lacks the feature where you hover over a window and it shows that window. Darn.

Color scheme is blue. It is surprisingly pleasant on the eyes.

There is actually a patched version of stasks that implements window peeking in a very hackish way. It sets the window temporarily to "always on top" and doesn't work for minimized windows. However, there's a proper highlight window effect built into KDE 4.3 by default. Here's a [demo]("http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ZqviTYwJa1E").

### Post by gtr32 on 2009-05-31
> **bizarrechaos said:**
> Sweet and simple

It is. Just an idea...if you added a conky script for the middle part, and put in some time updates for your location and couple others, that could be cool. It would require some tweaking to get them to exact location but that's the fun part...

I have this in my conky:

Dallas$alignr${exec env TZ=US/Central date --rfc-3339=seconds}
Munich$alignr${exec env TZ=Europe/Berlin date --rfc-3339=seconds}
Oulu$alignr${exec env TZ=Europe/Helsinki date --rfc-3339=seconds}
Singapore$alignr${exec env TZ=Asia/Singapore date --rfc-3339=seconds}

### Post by Viva on 2009-05-31
> **sox fan Matt said:**
> Indeed it is!  And I loaded up black text in at least the forums as well..TY TJ :)  Now, is there a script for the terminal to be black?

Go to Edit -> Profile Preferences -> Colurs in the terminal, disable "Use Colours in system theme' and choose a darker theme from the drop down menu below.
